'shared/' here means 'the flat styles bucket delivered as registry:style', not 'shared between components' — the candidate misread it. Splitting these into per-component folders would break the source<->target correspondence and churn the registry/copy handoff contract that AGENTS.md and context.md §3 mark as a deliberate, intentional contract. Not in scope to alter, and the fix is churn that fights the contract.

### R-077 · dry · /Users/voitz/Projects/diffgazer-workspace/apps/docs/public/schema/diffgazer.json, /Users/voitz/Projects/diffgazer-workspace/cli/add/src/context.ts, /Users/voitz/Projects/diffgazer-workspace/cli/add/src/commands/init.ts

But this is not a structural defect. The two artifacts serve genuinely different consumers and runtimes: the JSON Schema is the public, IDE-only autocomplete artifact served at a stable $id URL (draft-07, intentionally loose), while the Zod schema is the CLI's runtime validator (transforms/refinements that JSON Schema cannot encode). Maintaining a runtime validator plus a separately-published editor JSON Schema is the standard, accepted TS-ecosystem pattern, not a placement/naming/grouping/SRP/barrel/dead-code problem the sota-structure doctrine flags. The candidate's own evidence concedes the placement 'is defensible,' and the schemas are currently in sync — the cited harm (silent drift) is hypothetical/future, not a present defect with evidence. The proposed fix (add a zod-to-json-schema build step or a drift-guard test) is speculative enforcement/process tooling, i.e. churn + YAGNI, not a concrete structural correction. Low-signal for a convergence tail; reject.

(2) Policy-inverted: D1 and context.md:189-191 make the <component>-<part> compound prefix an EXEMPTION (files MAY use it), not a MANDATE. The actual D1 finding criterion is the inverse — path-echo (basename repeating a path segment) IS the finding. searchable-content.tsx does NOT path-echo select/; it names exactly one concept (its primary export), which context.md:186-188 says is a CORRECT basename. (3) The proposed fix (rename to select-searchable-content.tsx) would deliberately ADD a path-echo prefix — the exact pattern the audit is stripping everywhere else (digest F-023, F-047, F-048, F-126, R-008, R-068 all remove echoing prefixes). That is direction-fighting churn over a D7 lockstep registry-surface rename. (4) The 'search/searchable confusable pair' is weak: SelectSearch (input control) vs SearchableContent (listbox partitioner) are distinct concepts; adding the prefix would yield the MORE confusable select-search.tsx vs select-searchable-content.tsx.
round: 11

### R-096 · dry · /Users/voitz/Projects/diffgazer-workspace/cli/add/src/utils/hashing.ts, /Users/voitz/Projects/diffgazer-workspace/libs/registry/src/copy-bundle.ts, /Users/voitz/Projects/diffgazer-workspace/libs/registry/src/cli/integrity.ts, /Users/voitz/Projects/diffgazer-workspace/cli/add/src/commands/remove.ts, /Users/voitz/Projects/diffgazer-workspace/cli/add/src/commands/add/manifest.ts, /Users/voitz/Projects/diffgazer-workspace/cli/add/src/utils/transform.ts
cli/add sha256() is an uncaught third copy of @diffgazer/registry computeIntegrity in the same installer-runtime layer
Evidence: cli/add/src/utils/hashing.ts:3-5 defines sha256(content) => `sha256-${createHash("sha256").update(content).digest("hex")}`, byte-identical to libs/registry/src/copy-bundle.ts:47-48 computeIntegrity (exported on the @diffgazer/registry `.` subpath, package.json exports `.`) and to libs/registry/src/cli/integrity.ts:5-7. sha256 is consumed 5x in cli/add (commands/remove.ts:254, commands/add/manifest.ts:77,110,117,126). cli/add already imports VALUE symbols from registry (remove.ts:2 `import { createRemoveCommand, findOrphanedNpmDeps } from "@diffgazer/registry/cli"`), so reusing computeIntegrity is trivial. cli/add/src/utils/transform.ts:21 explicitly comments that sha256 and registry computeIntegrity are equivalent. This sits in the installer-runtime path — the SAME layer as registry's installer — so it does NOT cross the runtime/build-time boundary that integrity.ts:3-4 ("Intentionally duplicated so installer runtime and artifact generation stay decoupled") protects. The digest (F-001..F-257, R-001..R-095) never mentions sha256/computeIntegrity/hashing/integrity; F-081 covers a different (path-containment) registry triple.
Fix: Have cli/add consume the published computeIntegrity from @diffgazer/registry (the `.` subpath already exports it) and delete cli/add/src/utils/hashing.ts; update the 5 call sites in commands/remove.ts and commands/add/manifest.ts plus the now-stale comment in utils/transform.ts:21. CAVEAT: the equivalence is documented as intentional in two places (integrity.ts:3-4 and transform.ts:21); the registry-internal copy-bundle/integrity pair should stay split (runtime vs artifact-gen decoupling). Only the cli/add copy is a candidate for consolidation, and only because cli/add already depends on registry at the same layer. Owner may legitimately keep it as-is for the same decoupling reason — hence info severity.
Rejection reason: Real-but-intentional, would be churn. The three byte-identical sha256/computeIntegrity wrappers do exist (cli/add/src/utils/hashing.ts:3-5, libs/registry/src/copy-bundle.ts:47-48, libs/registry/src/cli/integrity.ts:5-7), but the duplication is explicitly documented as intentional in THREE places: integrity.ts:3-4 and copy-bundle.ts:45-46 ('Intentionally duplicated so installer runtime and artifact generation stay decoupled') and — decisively — transform.ts:18-21, which extends the exact rationale to cli/add's local helpers verbatim: 'Kept local on purpose. dgadd publishes as a self-contained npm bundle... Same decoupling rationale as sha256 (utils/hashing.ts) and registry computeIntegrity.' The candidate's central premise (that the cli/add copy 'does NOT cross the runtime/build-time boundary' and that 'cli/add already imports VALUE symbols from registry so reuse is trivial') is wrong: @diffgazer/registry is a DEVdependency of cli/add (package.json devDependencies), bundled INTO the dgadd binary at build time via tsup noExternal:[/^@diffgazer\/registry(\/.*)?$/]. The deliberate convention keeps tiny self-contained crypto one-liners local so the published binary does not couple to extra registry internals. A 1-line `sha256-${hash}` wrapper is not 'meaningful duplication' nor a 'real named concept' per the sota-structure extraction bar; consolidating it fights the documented decoupling. The candidate itself rates it info and concedes the owner may keep it. Intentional convention => reject.
round: 13

### R-097 · hygiene / docs-vs-reality · /Users/voitz/Projects/diffgazer-workspace/.gitignore
Root .gitignore `/specs/` pattern actively shadows the tracked specs/archive/ tree (gitignore-vs-tracked seam beyond F-204)
Evidence: Root `.gitignore:13` `/specs/` is an active root-anchored ignore (`git check-ignore -v specs/NEWFILE` => `.gitignore:13:/specs/`), yet `specs/archive/` is committed and tracked (`git ls-files specs/ | wc -l` => 61). NOTE ON OVERLAP: binding decision D8 already mandates deleting `specs/archive/` (and the AUDIT/OPUS/FIX files and dated `audits/`), and R-016 confirmed that deletion is safe. Once D8 runs, `/specs/` becomes a correct forward-looking ignore. So this is a transient pre-D8 inconsistency in the same family as F-204, not an independent new structural defect.
Fix: Fold into the D8 cleanup task: after deleting `specs/archive/` per D8, keep the `/specs/` ignore as the intended forward-looking guard (now correct). No separate action needed if D8 is executed; if D8 slips, note that `/specs/` currently shadows a tracked 61-file tree exactly as F-204 describes for the AUDIT files. No code change required in this round.
Rejection reason: Evidence is literally accurate (.gitignore:13 `/specs/`; `git check-ignore -v specs/NEWFILE` => `.gitignore:13:/specs/`; 61 files tracked under specs/archive/), and the specific line-13 `/specs/` pattern is not verbatim in any prior digest entry (F-204 enumerated only AUDIT_*/OPUS_AUDIT_*/FIX_SPEC_* lines 30-32; F-097 is libs/ui/specs/; F-088 is agent-specs/). BUT this names no independent actionable defect. Binding decision D8 already mandates deleting specs/archive/, and R-016 already confirmed that deletion is safe. The candidate's own fix concedes 'No separate action needed if D8 is executed... No code change required in this round' — once D8 runs, `/specs/` is a correct forward-looking guard. So this is a transient pre-D8 inconsistency in the same hygiene family as confirmed F-204, fully subsumed by D8 + R-016 + F-204; the only proposed action (note it in the D8 task) is redundant with already-binding scope and produces no new work. Fails the improve-vs-churn test: a finding whose fix is 'no change required' is not a standalone structural finding. Reject as substantive duplicate of the F-204 hygiene family + D8/R-016 coverage.
round: 15
